  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_136ea37c-d9ee-452f-8c63-e463bd67a659'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText14330905885745512782" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Go west. Capture Apollo before he can find the next oracle.<br />If you cannot bring him to me alive, kill him.</i>
</b><br /><br />Those were the orders my old enemy Nero had given to Meg McCaffrey. But why would an ancient Roman emperor zero in on Indianapolis? And now that I have made it here (still in the embarrassing form of Lester Papadopoulos), where is Meg?<br /><br />Meg, my demigod master, is a cantankerous street urchin. She betrayed me to Nero back at Camp Half-Blood. And while I'm mortal, she can order me to do anything . . . even kill myself. Despite all this, if I have a chance of prying her away from her villainous stepfather, I have to try.<br /><br />But I'm new at this heroic-quest business, and my father, Zeus, stripped me of all my godly powers. Oh, the indignities and pain I have already suffered! Untold humiliation, impossible time limits, life-threatening danger . . . Shouldn't there be a reward at the end of each completed task? Not just more deadly quests?<br /><br />I vow that if I ever regain my godhood, I will never again send a poor mortal on a quest. Unless it is really important. And unless I am sure the mortal can handle it. And unless I am pressed for time . . . or I really just don't feel like doing it myself. I will be <i>much</i> kinder and more generous than everyone is being to meâ€”especially that sorceress Calypso. What does Leo see in her, anyway?</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/764884-is-anyone-else-hoping-more-than-anything">Is anyone else hoping more than anything that Reyna becomes one of the main characters not only for this book but the rest of the series? I mean, come on, the girl is beyond awesome! Yeah, she&#39;s a prayer or and has responsibilities in New Rome, but hey you never know!</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_764884'><a id="like_count_community_question_764884" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/764884?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">67 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F30145666-the-dark-prophecy">like</a></span>

</li>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/764884-is-anyone-else-hoping-more-than-anything">See all 22 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/56018550-colinne-patrice"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1596832414i/56018550._UX100_CR0,2,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/56018550-colinne-patrice">Colinne Patrice</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes I would love that. Also something crossed my mind when I was re-reading the whole series: Venus told Reyna that she would not be loved by a demi-g<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">â€¦more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes I would love that. Also something crossed my mind when I was re-reading the whole series: Venus told Reyna that she would not be loved by a demi-god. Which might mean she'll fall in love with a god instead. And then the next book comes Apollo, falling from the sky, recounting how he has lost the two only people he ever truly loved. What if he met Reyna and the two fell for each other? She is awesome, I can see him falling for her no problem. Of course I don't think she would not be much impressed by him at first (notably his egomaniac side could be a downer) but if he proved his worth by reclaiming the oracles (without whining to much about it) she would probably start liking him, with her being a Roman and a sucker for duty and honour and all that...<br />Anyway I do hope that we see a lot of her in the future books, whether or not she ends up with Apollo.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1741575290" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1741575290?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1741575290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8763724702194815005"><blockquote>
  <i>I tried to think of a brilliant plan. Unfortunately, the only thing that came to mind was weeping in terror.</i>
</blockquote><br/>What an absolute dork. <b>I love him so much</b> â™¥<br/><br/>Honestly, Apollo is hands down my favourite character that Riordan has ever created. I know all of these books have the same light, humourous tone, but none of the others seem to make me laugh so much. Apollo is just so sassy and snarky, and his disdain for humans rings with hilarious truth.<br/><br/>I think I like these Apollo stories so much more beca</span>
  <span id="freeText8763724702194815005" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I tried to think of a brilliant plan. Unfortunately, the only thing that came to mind was weeping in terror.</i>
</blockquote><br />What an absolute dork. <b>I love him so much</b> â™¥<br /><br />Honestly, Apollo is hands down my favourite character that Riordan has ever created. I know all of these books have the same light, humourous tone, but none of the others seem to make me laugh so much. Apollo is just so sassy and snarky, and his disdain for humans rings with hilarious truth.<br /><br />I think I like these Apollo stories so much more because they feel the most unique. Many of the other voices - e.g. Percy Jackson and Magnus Chase - started to blend together after a little while, and their characters were hard to distinguish from one another. And the plots of the other books seemed to move in similar cycles of prophecy-quest-resolution, whereas this and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859.The_Hidden_Oracle__The_Trials_of_Apollo___1_" title="The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hidden Oracle</a> contained more surprises.<br /><br />Did I mention that it's full of laughs?<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Oh!" I said. "Um...nah." I leaned against the wall, hoping to look casual, attractive and suave. Unfortunately, I missed the wall.</i>
</blockquote><br />Also, I just kind of love that Apollo is a narcissistic ass. Don't get me wrong, I praised the Percy Jackson series for being all about how a seemingly regular kid discovers he is actually so much more and proceeds to become a hero. This is a great message. But sometimes there is just something so delightful about a character who is definitely NOT a hero and doesn't even pretend to be. <br /><br />In this book, Apollo has left Camp Half-Blood behind and is venturing out to restore Oracles and - hopefully - regain his place on Mount Olympus after Zeus cast him out and made him human. It is full of <b>adventure, haiku and mechanical dragons</b>, as well as some great LGBTQ+ representation (Apollo is, himself, bisexual). I can't wait for more.<br /><br />Quick note: there are spoilers for the Percy Jackson books, so maybe don't read this if you haven't read them yet.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8763724702194815005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1756670829" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1756670829" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1756670829?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141363974" href="/book/show/34472638-the-dark-prophecy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756670829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9015231449934344668"><b>Basically it's just the #1 fact of life that any book in the Camp Halfblood world CAN DO NO WRONG.</b> This was a completely fabulous sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859.The_Hidden_Oracle__The_Trials_of_Apollo___1_' title='The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo, #1) by Rick Riordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hidden Oracle</a>! Although I didn't like it <i>quite</i> as much because <b>(A)</b> it wasn't <i>as</i> hilarious, although still funny, and <b>(B)</b> the plot wasn't as exciting and twisty as the first one. But it was still an entirely solid read for me and I think I'm half in love with Apollo -- who is a DORK and narcissist and but what can you do. He's adorable.<br/><br/><b>I think Apollo's ch</b></span>
  <span id="freeText9015231449934344668" style="display:none"><b>Basically it's just the #1 fact of life that any book in the Camp Halfblood world CAN DO NO WRONG.</b> This was a completely fabulous sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859.The_Hidden_Oracle__The_Trials_of_Apollo___1_" title="The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hidden Oracle</a>! Although I didn't like it <i>quite</i> as much because <b>(A)</b> it wasn't <i>as</i> hilarious, although still funny, and <b>(B)</b> the plot wasn't as exciting and twisty as the first one. But it was still an entirely solid read for me and I think I'm half in love with Apollo -- who is a DORK and narcissist and but what can you do. He's adorable.<br /><br /><b>I think Apollo's character development is just so fabulous.</b> He's still 100% full of himself and really surprised when the world doesn't revolve around him (this happens to the best of us tbh), but he keeps getting more and more loyal to his demigod companions. And he's utter trash for looking after Meg. And, on occasion, he might even do something self-sacrificial instead of letting everyone else perish in his wake. #lovely <b>I do hate how they ALWAYS give him a rough time though!!</b> I mean, I get it...he's was horrible god. But like he tries so hard and Meg is so mean to him and Calypso and Leo give him 500% a rough time. Althoooooough. That is also what friends are for. And everyone they meet blames him for EVERYTHING. It's actually surprising that he stays in such good spirits about his own godliness when he's cleaning toilets and peeling carrots.<br /><br /><b>I'm still waiting to warm up to Meg though???</b> I wasn't really invested in her in book #1, and she just continues to be a rude little turnip. I suppose it's meant to be endearing??? I find the actual root vegetable more endearing. I guess I'm a fan of manners and kindness, both of which Meg is allergic to.<br /><br /><b>GREAT THINGS TO EXPECT:</b><br />â€¢ the unexpected; because seriously you have no idea what this book is going to throw at you next<br />â€¢ gods on facebook<br />â€¢ monsters, murder, and mayhem<br />â€¢ booby traps<br />â€¢ prophecies that nearly kill you<br />â€¢ tofu<br />â€¢ mechanical dragons that are designed like lego<br />â€¢ a house that only shows you the rooms it wants to and expands when requested<br />â€¢ griffins<br />â€¢ featuring f/f parent couple<br />â€¢ bisexual Apollo<br />â€¢ sass<br />â€¢ fighting<br />â€¢ SASSSSSSSSSS<br /><br /><br /><b>I laughed so much omg.</b> The lines are HYSTERICAL and I think Apollo's tendency to use "god like speech" but then mesh it with modern pop-culture references and narcissistic haikus is just the best thing since cupcakes were invented. I am such a fan omg. He's got a relaly different voice to Percy Jackson too, which is GREAT.<br /><br /><b>And I also love how the structure of these books are less like the PJO books.</b> They're on an adventure that continually unravels, so it's not the same-old-same-old plot set up (get a prophecy, assemble a team, go on a quest, nearly die, etc.) of the PJO books. It's just a bit refreshing and sets them apart.<br /><br /><b>BUT SHOULD YOU BE READING APOLLO IF YOU HAVEN'T READ THE PERCY JACKSON BOOKS?</b> Erm. No. There <i>are</i> spoilers for the Percy books. And even that aside, you wouldn't get a lot of the references/characters.<br /><br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: this was definitely a hilariously glorious sequel!</b> Maybe it wasn't as fast moving or exciting as other Halfblood books, and maaaaybe it dragged a bit in the middle. But it was still funny and used a LOT of the more obscure Greek myths so I was forced to <i>learn things</i>. How dare it. I'm definitely a huge fan of Apollo!! 10/10 will recommend giving Apollo a cookie and perhaps a break, but also it's hilarious to watch him suffer through being a human. <br /><br /><br /><b>*** QUOTES ***</b><br /><br /><blockquote>I tried to think of a brilliant plan. Unfortunately, the only thing that came to mind was weeping in terror.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>I wondered if Meg knew that [names redacted] had been beheaded for letting her escape. I decided not to mention it. If Meg was really curious, she could check their Facebook status updates.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Commodus blames me for his death," I said.<br />"Why?" Meg asked.<br />"Probably because I killed him."<br />"Ah." Leo nodded sagely. "That would do it.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"No sweat," Leo said. "I'll handle the first two hundred or so myself, then if I get tired--"<br />"Leo, stop." Calypso gave Emmie an apologetic frown. "He jokes more when he's nervous. He also jokes <i>worse</i> when he's nervous."<br />"I have no idea what you're talking about." Leo inserted carrot fangs into his mouth and snarled.<br />Meg almost choked on her stir-fry.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Oh!" I said. "Um...nah." I leaned against the wall, hoping to look casual, attractive and suave. Unfortunately, I missed the wall.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>My eyelids fluttered open. I sat up, groaning. When you are the sun god, it's a rare treat to be able to sleep late. Now here I was, a mere mortal, and people kept waking me up at the crack of dawn. I'd spent millennia <i>being</i> the crack of dawn. I was tired of it.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="9015231449934344668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17834927136429158438"><b>
  <blockquote>â€œPlease get off!â€ the trooper wailed. â€œPlease and thank you!â€</blockquote>

The tone of this book is as good as the first book but the pace is quite slow. Apollo reminded me of Deadpool talking with readers with his sarcastic tone. His develo</span>
  <span id="freeText17834927136429158438" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>â€œPlease get off!â€ the trooper wailed. â€œPlease and thank you!â€</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494436711i/22714689._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I hysterically laughed my ass off while I was reading this book on the BTS. The Dark Prophecy picks up after what happened in The Hidden Oracle. Lester, aka Apollo, teamed up with Leo and his girlfriend and comes to Indianapolis to pursue the prophecy he was bestowed. The tone of this book is as good as the first book but the pace is quite slow. Apollo reminded me of Deadpool talking with readers with his sarcastic tone. His development is promiment and what I have expected. His attitude is frivolous as always, you know, but it's the point of this series why it's so much differrent from the Percy Jackson series despite the fact that it's sharing the same world-building.<br><br>Leo, on the other hand, is a solid character in this book. Although he is oafish at times, he still got my attention as he did in The Heroes of Olympus. Moreover, the emperor, Commodus, is exactly a narcissistic character that I almost died of laughing, and I think he might be my favorite villain of all time. Meg is one of the best protagonists I've ever seen. From the first half of this book, I thought her character was such a typical heroine, and I had no idea how wrong I was until the very end of this book. She's so intricate !<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>â€œHe looked like a hallucinating ballerina in boxer shorts,â€ </blockquote>
</b><br><br>The griffins are excellent that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I almost cried when he loses his mate. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> However, sometimes I didn't get what Lester were talking about, I knew it's all his music or rhyme, but it's also one of the reasons why I didn't enjoy this fully. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494514373ra/22723385.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending of this led me to the long wait for the next book. Yet I have a gut feeling it's gonna be as exciting as the fourth book of the Percy Jackson series.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>â€œBeing productive. Ugh. It's such a human concept. It implies you have limited time (LOL) and have to work hard to make something happen (double LOL).â€ </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494514373ra/22723386.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2214189260" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Ahmed  Ejaz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53694260-ahmed-ejaz"><img alt="Ahmed  Ejaz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598778737p2/53694260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2214189260?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmed  Ejaz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmed  Ejaz" href="/user/show/53694260-ahmed-ejaz">Ahmed  Ejaz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53694260-ahmed-ejaz?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53694260-ahmed-ejaz?shelf=full-lengths">full-lengths</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2214189260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6198599991741355075"><i>
  <b>Most of you must have gotten by now that </b>
</i> I have gotten <i>completely</i> addicted to Rick Riordan. This is the 12th book I have read by him and I read the previous eleven books almost in row. And the thought of <i>any</i> regret didn't even pass before me.<br/><br/>Well, for this book it was much better than the last one. It was more gripping and more interesting. The only thing which was missing here was Percbeth!! Annabeth didn't even appear in the last one. She is helping her relative or something....WHATEVER! </span>
  <span id="freeText6198599991741355075" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Most of you must have gotten by now that </b>
</i> I have gotten <i>completely</i> addicted to Rick Riordan. This is the 12th book I have read by him and I read the previous eleven books almost in row. And the thought of <i>any</i> regret didn't even pass before me.<br /><br />Well, for this book it was much better than the last one. It was more gripping and more interesting. The only thing which was missing here was Percbeth!! Annabeth didn't even appear in the last one. She is helping her relative or something....WHATEVER! I really want PERCBETH IN THE NEXT BOOK! <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> Itâ€™s not how long you live that matters. Itâ€™s what you live for.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote>I loved Apollo! His sense of humour is unique in the entire series. He is changing. But I was enjoying his whining more than this. Anyway, I don't mind how he is doing.<br />&gt;&gt;The scene of revelation of Prophecy here was the best. I loved that.<br />&gt;&gt;In the Blood of Olympus, I was glad that Leo had rescued Calypso. And I was really looking forward to their proper relationship here. But in this book, the spark that should have been in their relationship was drastically missing. I didn't feel liking this ship the way I liked in Heros of Olympus series. <br />&gt;&gt;And...wow! One of my favourite characters from Percy Jackson and the Olympians series is BACK!!!!! Wowowowowow!! Can't wait. Not a chance after the interpretation of the Prophecy.<br /><br />Regardless of the fact, this book follows the formula of previous books, regardless of it being very predictable (at least for me), regardless of everything, I <i>enjoyed</i> this book. How can you not LOL at his humor? He's got a powerful tool to enchant his readers. And that is <i>freakin'</i> humor! <br /><br /><b>P.S</b><br />So, this is the last book I have read for now. I won't be reading novels for a little long time in future because I am getting very busy. Exams, studies..you know. But I will be reading comics and short stories in this time as they are very short and less addictive than novels. <i>*something is better than nothing*</i><br /><br />14 December, 2017</span>
  <a data-text-id="6198599991741355075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Maureen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10762033-maureen"><img alt="Maureen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398557569p2/10762033.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maureen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maureen" href="/user/show/10762033-maureen">Maureen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2025983982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11574705047553861822">I honestly don't know how Rick Riordan's books keep getting funnier but they do somehow. Being in Apollo's head, while annoying at times, is hilarious. <br/>I enjoyed this book but didn't *love* it. I think Apollo just doesn't appeal to me as much as Percy or any of the other Demigods, but it's really interesting and entertaining to have a new perspective. I'm excited to see where it goes next!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6064730638296825917"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"I, the most important passenger, the youth who had once been the glorious god Apollo, was forced to sit in the back of the dragon."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505397898ra/23922438.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>More than once while reading I've had to ponder: <b>Am I getting too old for Percy Jackson?</b> That thought filled me with such terror I had to drink from my Butterbeer cup and gaze up at my wall of Taylor Swift posters to confirm that, yes, I was a stinkin'no-good millennial who blows her money on stupid shit instead helping the economy.<br/><br/>But as I read on, I r</span>
  <span id="freeText6064730638296825917" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I, the most important passenger, the youth who had once been the glorious god Apollo, was forced to sit in the back of the dragon."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505397898ra/23922438.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>More than once while reading I've had to ponder: <b>Am I getting too old for Percy Jackson?</b> That thought filled me with such terror I had to drink from my Butterbeer cup and gaze up at my wall of Taylor Swift posters to confirm that, yes, I was a stinkin'no-good millennial who blows her money on stupid shit instead helping the economy.<br><br>But as I read on, I realized the problem wasn't meâ€”well, not <i>all</i> me anywayâ€”it's Apollo. <b>I can't stand the whiny human-god.</b> He was great in small doses like with the previous series, but being in his head for 300+ pages is <b>agonizing.</b> All he does is complain about how great he used to be, then sulk about his powerlessness. <br><br>I felt like going Kaz Brekker on his assâ€”"You think you know what pain looks like? Then he would paint a picture for them using his fists." Obviously, this is a very subjective opinion. Lots of reviewers adore Apollo, some actually preferring this series over its predecessors because of him.<br><br>Stale jokes asideâ€”I didn't laugh out loud <i>once</i> while readingâ€”the other wonderful stoutheart primary character we're supposed to root for is Meg. <b>Rude, bratty, crude Meg.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407600433ra/10744798.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am in no way putting down her character arc. I think it's awesome that her relationship with Nero represents a soft abusiveness, one based on emotional manipulation and attacking her self-esteem instead of hard fists, and lots of kids and younger teens will be able to relate and learn from it. But as an adult-in-training, I feel it could have been written with more finesse. Basically I've read better.<br><br>And someone needs to teach Riordan how to <b>properly withhold information without stabbing a big red flag in the narrative soil every time.</b> It was like that in the Heroes of Olympus series, too. A character would think of something foreboding, then right when readers are about to see what the object it, the train of thought snaps off as the characters resolutely thinks, "It can't be THAT monster/Thinking about THAT monster will just make me more scared." Here, the monster's identity is concealed by the Rule of Voldemortâ€”if you say his name, he can and will track you down.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505362146i/23918383.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>There are positives.</b> Thumbs up for diversity in the form of lesbian parents, Apollo's bisexuality/pansexuality, and fleshing out token minorities. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26252859.The_Hidden_Oracle__The_Trials_of_Apollo___1_" title="The Hidden Oracle (The Trials of Apollo, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hidden Oracle</a>, while retaining many of these features, didn't quite handle it as well, so yay improvement! <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Another nod of approval towards Leo and Calypso. They deal with normal relationship problems, even after their flight into the sunset. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505362014ra/23918354.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505362014ra/23918356.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(Still think Riordan did a 180 on her personality in order to shove them together in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12127810.The_House_of_Hades__The_Heroes_of_Olympus___4_" title="The House of Hades (The Heroes of Olympus, #4) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The House of Hades</a>, but my babies are undeniably adorable) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I'll continue the series because Riordan is the self-deprecating love I keep running back to, but my expectations will remain at a reasonable height below my ankle socks.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1394786091" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of The Hidden Oracle</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1663791909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1663791909" />
    <a title="Drew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22104588-drew"><img alt="Drew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498412758p2/22104588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1663791909?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew" href="/user/show/22104588-drew">Drew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1663791909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer143873769227915374">I'm so tired of the shameless liberal advertising in books lately. I'm seeing it in nearly every YA book I pick up, but reading it in a middle grade book, a book meant for children, was the last straw. It prompted me to finally write something about this vastly growing issue.<br/><br/>There I was, happily content to be reading some fun Rick Riordan mythology again, when suddenly a huge sign with the words LIBERAL BRAINWASHING AHEAD popped up. You know when you're in the middle of watching a YouTube video </span>
  <span id="freeText143873769227915374" style="display:none">I'm so tired of the shameless liberal advertising in books lately. I'm seeing it in nearly every YA book I pick up, but reading it in a middle grade book, a book meant for children, was the last straw. It prompted me to finally write something about this vastly growing issue.<br /><br />There I was, happily content to be reading some fun Rick Riordan mythology again, when suddenly a huge sign with the words LIBERAL BRAINWASHING AHEAD popped up. You know when you're in the middle of watching a YouTube video and a thirty second ad interrupts that just about ruins the whole video? Yeah, that's how it felt when Riordan decided to throw some of his political views into this book.<br /><br />The worst part is this book is for kids. <b>Children are reading this.</b> Children as young as eight should not be subject to adult matters - such as a lesbian couple, which this book promoted in chapter six.<br /><br />Would people be okay if someone wrote about a drag queen in a children's book? What if child characters went to a strip club? No? Then why, I ask, is it okay to put a lesbian couple, portray two women living together, and promote your own shameless political agenda, in a book meant for young, easily impressionable minds?<br /><br />Whether you support the LGBT+ community or not is beside the point. People have the right to hold whatever opinions they want. But I think all adult matters should be kept out of kids' entertainment, and it's horrible when adults try to sneak it in because they think it's "funny" or they're trying to push their own personal agenda.<br /><br />War, alcoholism, suicide, sex, prostitution, or any other adult things should not be put in children's books. Adults keep those topics away from children for a reason - they're too much for them to handle. And I don't think sexual identification should be put in children's books either, when the young minds reading them haven't even begun to develop sexually yet.<br /><br />Look, my whole problem wasn't even that there were gay characters in this book. My problem was that Riordan was <b>so obviously including them just for the sake of "representation."</b> Representation of different groups is a great thing, and I love when I come across a genuinely diverse bookâ€¦ but when the author is trying so hard to make their book diverse to earn brownie points, it comes across as unnatural and takes away from the story.<br /><br />Anyway, the gay thing is so overdone by now it's getting ridiculous. It's one thing when you have an actual gay character like Radu from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190613.And_I_Darken__The_Conqueror_s_Saga___1_" title="And I Darken (The Conqueror's Saga, #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">And I Darken</a> and it makes sense for them to be gay. But when you throw in a gay character just to get your LGBT+ brownie points and they're only in the book for, like, two seconds? If I were gay, I would be insulted by this "representation."<br /><br />Please, move on to something new.</span>
  <a data-text-id="143873769227915374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16284563430695977164">The Dark Prophecy (The Trials of Apollo, #2), Rick Riordan<br/>The Dark Prophecy is an American fantasy novel based on Greek and Roman mythology written by Rick Riordan. It was published on May 2, 2017, and is the second book in The Trials of Apollo series.<br/>Six weeks after losing Meg McCaffrey to Nero and receiving the first prophecy, Apollo, Leo, Festus and Calypso are headed on a journey to stop Nero and the Triumvirate from controlling all of the oracles. Apollo has a vision that Margeret was sent </span>
  <span id="freeText16284563430695977164" style="display:none">The Dark Prophecy (The Trials of Apollo, #2), Rick Riordan<br />The Dark Prophecy is an American fantasy novel based on Greek and Roman mythology written by Rick Riordan. It was published on May 2, 2017, and is the second book in The Trials of Apollo series.<br />Six weeks after losing Meg McCaffrey to Nero and receiving the first prophecy, Apollo, Leo, Festus and Calypso are headed on a journey to stop Nero and the Triumvirate from controlling all of the oracles. Apollo has a vision that Margeret was sent to Indianapolis by Nero with orders to kill Apollo, so the trio travels there to find the next Oracle. They are rescued from attacking blemmyae by Hemithea and invited into the Waystation, a sentient building created by the minor goddess Britomartis and is used as a home for demigods, runaways, Hunters of Artemis, etc. Apollo recalls offering to turn Hemithea into a goddess but having his gift rejected to join the Hunters of Artemis. He learns that she is in a relationship with Josephine and the two of them have sacrificed their immortality as Hunters for love and are living as mortals. Their adopted daughter Georgina went missing after searching for the Oracle of Trophonius to receive a prophecy to prevent the Triumvirate from taking their animals. Instead, she receives a message that damages her mind and causes her to wander away. Britomaris, who is also the goddess of nets and the mother of all griffins, issues Apollo and Calypso a quest to rescue the griffins stolen by Commodus the next morning. Apollo has a dream that Meg Mccaffrey escaped Nero and is now on the run. The duo manages to rescue the griffins but is cornered by Lityerses, Commodus' right hand man. Meg McCaffrey arrives and duels with Lityerses until Apollo releases the rest of the caged animals. <span id="freeTextContainer1756482827993784203">Still funny and entertaining, but not as funny and entertaining as book one. I was a little disappointed because one of my favorite aspects of book one was that Apollo interacted with his kids, and I was fully expecting a couple of them to join him on this quest (namely Will with Nico tagging along). And while I did get familiar faces none of his kids joined him.<br/><br/>However, many new characters are introduced who I grew to like.   <span id="freeText1756482827993784203" style="display:none">Still funny and entertaining, but not as funny and entertaining as book one. I was a little disappointed because one of my favorite aspects of book one was that Apollo interacted with his kids, and I was fully expecting a couple of them to join him on this quest (namely Will with Nico tagging along). And while I did get familiar faces none of his kids joined him.<br /><br />However, many new characters are introduced who I grew to like. Then we have one of my babies who finally returned. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Oh Leo, how I've missed you. Calypso is cool too, but Leo is my baby. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Meg returns of course and she's grown on me even more in this book. Actually, one of my favorite aspects of this book was Apollo and Meg's friendship. Different from book one in which all Meg does is boss Apollo around they have evolved into a camaraderie where they work together. Meg will still sometimes say a command, but it's not out of cruelty or punishment. Apollo genuinely cares about Meg, and vice versa, and having them protect one another warms my heart. <br /><br />And Apollo, oh man, you're still so egotistical and funny. He's the tiniest bit less self-centered, but he still mostly believes the world revolves around him. I think it's because he's used to riding the sun chariot, and the Earth revolves around the sun (and therefore him). Still he shows compassion. He has regrets and cares for those around him. <br /><br />The quest in this book, while interesting, was not one of my favorites. The next quest seems like it will be more entertaining. Especially because we'll get to see even more of my babies! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ALSO GROVER IS HERE!!!!! I've missed Grover and I honestly can't wait to see how he'll deal with the troublesome duo of Apollo and Meg lmao. I'm sure he'll have his work cut out for him with this escort. Bad shit will definitely go down. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11811599268544026103"><br/>This book is such an <b>absolute delight</b>. It's one of those things in life you thought you really didn't need until it enters your life and proves you completely wrong. Then, you vociferously realize that you need more of it, NOW. <br/><br/>In a world where hatred, suffering, and oppression seem to proliferate exponentially (at least in the news, no thanks to the orange cheeto occupying the white house and his enablers in the house and senate), this book is a much-needed tonic of unbridled laughter, sass, an</span>
  <span id="freeText11811599268544026103" style="display:none"><br>This book is such an <b>absolute delight</b>. It's one of those things in life you thought you really didn't need until it enters your life and proves you completely wrong. Then, you vociferously realize that you need more of it, NOW. <br><br>In a world where hatred, suffering, and oppression seem to proliferate exponentially (at least in the news, no thanks to the orange cheeto occupying the white house and his enablers in the house and senate), this book is a much-needed tonic of unbridled laughter, sass, and joy. The book is low-stakes (in terms of stress) while being completely unpredictable. Again, didn't realize how much I needed that. <br><br>It is no secret that Rick Riordan has a magical gift for writing characters that one learns to grow and care deeply about (why I am such a big fan of him). And he does it again in this series. I LOVE THE CHARACTER OF APOLLO SO MUCH. &lt;3 I am just so invested in all of these rad, beautiful characters in this messy, incredible world that Riordan has created. ALL OF THE MEMORIES AND FEELS. (<b>For those who have not read the Percy Jackson and Heroes of Olympus series, reading these books will give you major spoilers.</b> You must go read them. Now.) <br><br>I think the older I get, the more I grow to appreciate how <b>radical</b> a project that Riordan has undertaken--to write stories where people of color, womxn, LGBTQ+, and other marginalized peoples are <i>normalized</i> and celebrated. That everyone can be a fantastic demigod, hero, or even a god. And along the way, Rick Riordan teaches me so much about mythology without me ever even realizing it. <br><br>As Roxane Gay puts it, "we deserve to be entertained even as the world burns. There is enough room in our collective imagination to care about the fate of the world <i>and</i>" the fate of Apollo and the whole motley crew. And care we do. <br><br><u>before reading</u><br>Q: why do I ALWAYS read Rick Riordan books right when they come out?! <br><br>I should stop that practice because it ALWAYS ends up with me staring at the next release date like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442730619ra/16273855.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>*crying at the 1 year wait*</i></span>

I have a review up for the first book, the one before this review on my blog. I will also warn that there may be a few minor spoilers for book one, but if youâ€™re not too bothered by that then read ahead, friends!<br /><br />The Dark Prophecy may be my least favourite of Rick Riordanâ€™s books ever. It was just not enjoyable for me. I felt the storyline just fell flat. There wasnâ€™t as much going on and at times it felt that nothing was furthering this story. It was annoying, honestly, and made for a relatively boring plot line. I mean, there were some interesting points but at some points, I felt that there were too many storylines happening within this particular one.<br /><br />The second book in the Trials of Apollo picks up soon after the first book. We have Leo, Calypso and Apollo ride off on Festus, a mechanical dragon that Leo helped in The Heroesâ€™ of Olympus. Apollo must defeat the next emperor in order to reclaim his oracle. Honestly, I donâ€™t have much of an idea of what really went down in this book. I was pretty confused and Iâ€™m not sure if itâ€™s because I read the book fast or simply because it wasnâ€™t explained well. I feel that Rick Riordan really used his name to push this crappy book through.<br /><br />L I K E S<br />âœ— FAST STORYLINE<br /><br />I realize I did just complain about this but the storyline was fast. It was action filled and I think thatâ€™s what led to a lot of my confusion throughout the book. I typically love when a lot happens in a book but I just wish that this one had slowed down a little. Maybe itâ€™s because Iâ€™m older but I just feel like these characters deserve a nice nap. I also got lost in the Greek/Roman mythology and kept jumbling them.<br /><br />Reading back I realized that this should be in dislikes but I did enjoy the storyline.<br /><br />âœ— GOOD CHARACTER DEVELOPMENT<br /><br />Every character but our lead had some great character development. Theyâ€™re all growing and realizing things (wow, Kylie Jenner is up in here). A lot of characters come to a standstill in Rick Riordanâ€™s second books, in my opinion, but I feel like the cast, overall, was being pushed forward which made for an obviously more enjoyable story.<br /><br />âœ— A F/F COUPLE<br /><br />Why did one of my favourite couples have to be in the worst books? I have a theory that f/f couples are literally the best to read about. They always make me giddy and the couple in The Dark Prophecy was no different. Emmie and Josephine are ex-Hunters of Artemis who fell in love with each other and left. It is bittersweet. They take care of the Waystation now, where Hunters drop in every now and again and help care for them. I loved it. Their added storyline was one that made me really happy to read, but also really sad.<br /><br />Iâ€™m still stoked that there was an f/f couple. It just felt like we were starting from scratch. At times his voice throughout the novel grated on me as well. I read all three books very close together and this was the only one that did that to me.<br /><br />Apollo is obviously going to be a jerk and will not change 100% by the end of this series, Iâ€™m just still so annoyed because he had gained some sense of caring throughout The Hidden Oracle and The Dark Prophecy had it gone.<br /><br />I did not read a whole book to have my time wasted in a second, no way.<br /><br />âœ— AT TIMES IT FEELS LIKE THE CHARACTERS FROM OTHER BOOKS TAKE OVER THE STORY<br /><br />I can see what Rick Riordan is trying to do, heâ€™s trying to show fans of his other series the happy endings of the previous characters they wrote. However, it just felt weak at times. Maybe itâ€™s because I donâ€™t care about either Leo or Calypso but it felt that at times their bickering and post-war romance took over. I really didnâ€™t care. Obviously, the previous book had included Percy Jackson, which I had no problems but, it just felt different here.<br /><br />It really just felt like Rick Riordan was trying too hard, that he had no idea what he was doing throughout this book.<br /><br />Overall, The Dark Prophecy isnâ€™t a bad book despite all my complaining. I did enjoy it but after reading every other of Rick Riordanâ€™s books it just didnâ€™t live up to the standards I had for this. I donâ€™t know if itâ€™s the voice of Apollo completely or simply the fact that Iâ€™m a picky bitch. Who knows, hopefully, the third book is better or I may just have to give up on this series.<br /><br /><a>Also, if you're looking to buy any books over at Book Depository, feel free to use my affiliate link!   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zPmUrxtKlrWorcHjkVmutGzXQiN91udqMSDm8UXnOSz+JqzJqLc2U7hbZ3x+OubhZq+zIvzji4Tsw5VyP/Z73Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }
